тАШрдиреВ рдорд░реНрддрдГ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкреНрддрд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рд╡рд╕рд┐рд╖реНрдард╕реНрдпрд╛рд░реНрд╖рдВ рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднрдВ рд╡реИрд╖реНрдгрд╡рдореН ред ‘рдиреВ рдорд░реНрддрдГ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рдЙрдХреНрдереНрдпреЗ рдЕрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рд╡рд╛рдХрд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░ рдЗрджрдВ рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдореН ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рддрдВ рдЪ - тАШ рдЛрддреБрд░реНрдЬрдирд┐рддреНрд░реА рдиреВ рдорд░реНрддреЛ рднрд╡рд╛ рдорд┐рддреНрд░рдГ ’ ( рдЖрд╢реНрд╡. рд╢реНрд░реМ. рем. рез) рдЗрддрд┐ редред

Jamison Brereton

100 (616)
Vis╠гn╠гu
Vasiс╣гс╣нha Maitr─Бvaruс╣Зi
7 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The hymn begins conventionally enough, with a mortal offering sacrifice to the god (vs. 1) and a request for gifts in return (vs. 2). Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs three strides are the subject of the following two, responsive verses (3тАУ4). Verse 3d also introduces the theme of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs name, which is the subject of the last two real verses of the hymn (5тАУ6, since vs. 7 is merely a repetition of the final verse of VII.99). The enigmatic epithet ┼Ыipiviс╣гс╣нa╠Б found in the last verse of the last hymn (VII.99.7) is, as it were, interrogated in these verses. In verse 6 the poet, who boasts that he knows the hidden patterns, sets out to proclaim the godтАЩs name, while addressing him as ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa, and then asks in the next verse whether the godтАЩs own proclamation of himself as ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa was meant to be ignored or passed over. The poet then mysteriously alludes to two different forms of the god, which may (or may not) correspond to two different names. The hymn does not resolve these questions, perhaps leaving the shadowy figure of Viс╣гс╣Зu to be fully developed in the ensuing centuries.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe mortal desirous of wealth quickly obtains it who presents (offerings) to the widely-renownedViс╣гс╣Зu, who worships him with entirely devoted mind, who adores so great a benefactor of mankind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Withentirely devoted mind: i.e. with united praise, saha├▒cat─Б stotreс╣Зa

Jamison Brereton

Now the mortal desiring to gain gets his share, if he does pious service to wide-ranging Viс╣гс╣Зu,

will set the sacrifice in motion with fully focused mind, and will seek to attract here such a one, favorable to men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The meter of the first p─Бda is badly off and is not easily fixable. See Oldenberg

He suggests a distracted reading of n┼л╠Бand records the suggestion that m├бrto should be emended to m├бrti yo, which Holland & van Nooten Rig Veda edition print as their text. If both are adopted (distracted n┼л╠Бand m├бrti yo; so Arnold p. 310), the line achieves 11 syllables, but the price may be too high, esp. as the light fourth syllable would be unusual.

Although d├бyate generally means тАШdistribute (goods to someone else)тАЩ, e.g., I.68.6 t├бsmai тАж ray├нс╣Г dayasva, in a few passages it seems to have adopted the more тАЬmiddleтАЭ meaning тАШreceive/take a shareтАЩ, perhaps adjusted to the model of other words of sharing, esp. bh├бjate тАШreceive a shareтАЩ versus act. bh├бjati тАШshare out, distribute sharesтАЩ. See Got┼Н (1st Kl., 172-73), whose tr. of this passage is close to mine. As noted ad II.33.10, I do not subscribe to Got┼НтАЩs separation of forms of d├бyate into two separate roots.

The three subsequent p─Бdas (bcd) state the conditions under which the mortal in p─Бda a will receive the longed-for share. They are marked by the rel. prn. y├бс╕е in b and c; adopting RenouтАЩs strategy I have rendered them as conditionals (тАЬifтАЭ) for clarity, rather than as straight rel. clauses (тАЬwhoтАЭ). Unfortunately I donтАЩt think my tr. makes it clear that cd are parallel to b, rather than being part of a resumed main clause, and I would now slightly emend the tr. to тАЬтАж, if he will set тАж and will seek тАжтАЭ). The apparent non-parallelism is exacerbated by the fact that the verbs of c and d (y├бj─Бte and ─Бv├нv─Бs─Бt respectively) are subjunctives, whereas d─Б╠Б┼Ыat in b should be the injunctive to the thematic pres. d─Б╠Б┼Ыati, which elsewhere attests a real subjunctive (d─Б╠Б┼Ы─Бt). Hoffmann discusses just this passage (Inj. 238), suggesting that in such contexts the indicative present, injunctive, and subjunctive overlap in usage. 130

Griffith

NE’ER doth the man repent, who, seeking profit, bringeth his gift to the far-striding Visnu.
He who adoreth him with all his spirit winneth himself so great a benefactor.

Grassmann

Der Mann, der Gut begehrt, bereut es nimmer, wenn Vischnu, dem weitschreitenden, er huldigt, Und ihn verehrt mit achtendem Gem├╝the, f├╝r sich gewinnend einen so gewalt’gen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬViс╣гс╣Зu, granter of desires, show to us that favourable disposition which is benevolent to all, unmixed(with exception), so that there may be to us the attainment of easily-acquire, ample, steed-comprising,all-delighting riches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Granter of desires: evay─Бvan: from eva = obtainable, desires;

Y─Бvan = who enables toobtain

Jamison Brereton

You, Viс╣гс╣Зu, traveling your waysтАФgive benevolent thought destined for all people, concentrated thought,
so that you will give us our fill of abundant welfare, of greatly glittering wealth in horses.

Griffith

Thou, Visnu, constant in thy courses, gavest good-will to all men, and a hymn that lasteth,
That thou mightst move us to abundant comfort of very splendid wealth with store of horses.

Geldner

English translation:

Jamison Brereton

Three times did the quick god stride with his greatness across this earth worth a hundred verses.
Let Viс╣гс╣Зu be preeminent, stronger than the strong, for vibrant is the
name of this stalwart one.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Flg. a suggestion by Geldner (n. 3a, though not reflected in his tr.), I take eс╣г├бin p─Бda a (also 4a) as belonging to the stem eс╣г├б- тАШquickтАЩ, which is used several times of Viс╣гс╣Зu in the gen. expression v├нс╣гс╣Зor eс╣г├бsya (II.34.11, VII.40.5, VIII.20.3), in which confusion with the nom. pronominal eс╣г├б(с╕е) (possible here) is excluded.

The hapax ┼Ыat├бrcas- is problematic. The Pp analyses the 2nd member as arcasam, but Wackernagel (AiG I.318) points out that the sandhi between the cmpd members would require rather -с╣Ыcasam. However, Oldenberg disputes this, claiming that it would then have to be written (тАЬтАж geschrieben werden m├╝ssenтАЭ) *┼Ыat├бс╣Ыcasam , though itтАЩs not clear to me why. Interpr. differ significantly: S─Бyaс╣Зa. glosses with arcis-.

Oldenberg posits a masc. s-stem *arc├бs- тАШsingerтАЩ, comparing VI.34.3 y├бdi stot─Б╠Бraс╕е ┼Ыat├бс╣Г y├бt sah├бsraс╣Г gс╣Ыс╣З├бnti тАЬWhen a hundred, when a thousand praisers sing to him тАж,тАЭ an interpr. followed by Geldner – though the connection between the two passages seems tenuous to me. By contrast, Renou tr. тАЬau cent ├йclats,тАЭ perhaps flg. S─Бyaс╣Зa.тАЩs arc├нs-. Since an infinitival dat. с╣Ыc├бse тАШto praise, for chanting (praise)тАЩ is found in VI.39.5 and VII.61.6, it seems reasonable to take the underlying stem с╣Ыcas- as the base here, as Grassmann does, glossing тАШhundertfach zu preisenтАЩ. My тАШworth a hundred versesтАЩ is close to that, though perhaps тАШpraises, chantsтАЩ would be better.

Because of the lack of accent on asya, it should be pronominal, not adjectival; I would adjust the tr. to тАЬof him, the stalwart.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis Viс╣гс╣Зu traversed the earth for a dwelling which he was desirous of giving to his eulogist; firm arethe people who are his praisers; he who is the engenderer of good has made a spacious dwelling (for hisworshippers).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which he was desirous of giving: manuс╣гe da┼Ыasyan = stuvate devagaс╣З─Бya, to the company ofgods praising him– Viс╣гс╣Зu having taken the three worlds from the Asuras to give to them; the engenderer ofgood: or, to whom belong fortunate births

Jamison Brereton

Quick Viс╣гс╣Зu strode across this earth for a dwelling place for Manu, showing his favor.
Firmly fixed are his peoples, (even) the weak. He, affording good birth, has made (them) wide dwelling.

Jamison Brereton Notes

By concentrating Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs strides in the first p─Бda of 4, the poet is free to express the aim of Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs action – creating space and dwelling places for the people

– in the rest of the vs. As Geldner points out (n. 4c), asya can refer either to Viс╣гс╣Зu or to Manu, although in actuality this may not matter. It may be an instance of тАЬtrickle-downтАЭ ownership: Viс╣гс╣Зu makes a dwelling place for Manu, and in turn ManuтАЩs people also get firmly planted. Or, Manu and the people may both be under Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs auspices.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted in the published introduction, vss. 3 and 4 are responsive. The first p─Бda of 4 concentrates the essence of the 1st two p─Бdas of 3, substituting v├н cakrame (of 3b) for tr├нr dev├бс╕е (in 3a) at the beginning of the p─Бda. This phrase, tr├нr dev├бс╕е, is short a syllable; Oldenberg suggests reading t╬Зrir, but this seems unlikely: I donтАЩt know of any other disyllabic readings of this extremely common numeral (either as 1st cmpd member tri- or adverbial tr├нs). I suggest rather that the metrically disturbed opening draws attention to the beginning of this set of paired vss. by being flawed and is тАЬrepairedтАЭ by 4a. See similar remarks about 3c and 5c ad vs. 5.

Griffith

Over this earth with mighty step strode Visnu, ready to give it for a home to Manu.
In him the humble people trust for safety: he, nobly born, hath made them spacious dwellings.

Dieser Vishnu hat diese Erde ausgeschritten zum Landbesitz f├╝r Manu, um ihm gef├дllig zu sein. Ans├дssig wurden dessen besitzlose Leute. Er, der gute Geburt gibt, schuf weite Wohnstatt.

Grassmann

Hinschreitend ging durch diese Erde Vischnu, der Gott dem Menschen sie zur Wohnung schenkend; Gesichert stehn die M├дnner, die ihn preisen; der gutes wirkt, er schaffte weiten Wohnsitz.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬResplendent Viс╣гс╣Зu, I, the master of the offering, knowing the objects that are to be known, glorifytoday your name; I who am feeble, praise you who are powerful, dwelling in a remote region of this worlс╕НтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

N─Бm─Бryaс╕е ┼Ыaс╣Гs─Бmi = I the lord, praise your name; S─Бmaveda has a different reading: pra tat te adyahavyam ─Бryaс╕е ┼Ыaс╣Гs─Бmi = I the lord, offer you today an oblation;

S┼лrya = sv─Бm─л stutin─Бm haviс╣г─Бm v─Б,you master of the praises or of the oblation which may mean Viс╣гс╣Зu or perhaps, the yajam─Бna

Jamison Brereton

This name of yours, o ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa, of you the stranger do I proclaim today, I who know the (hidden) patterns.
I hymn you, the strongтАФI, less strongтАФyou who rule over this dusky realm in the distance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On the name ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa, see comm. ad VII.99.4. Note that Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАЩs name was already celebrated in 3d, though the actual name is not mentioned there.

The syntactic affiliation of ary├бс╕е is disputed: the question is whether it depends on vay├║n─Бni or simply picks up te in the previous p─Бda. With Geldner and Renou I follow the latter course; Renou argues cogently that vay├║na- тИЪvid does not normally have a тАЬr├йgime ext├йrieurтАЭ (though I.72.7, II.19.3 appear to be exceptions). I would 131 further add that since ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa seems a type of тАЬsecret name,тАЭ referring to Viс╣гс╣Зu as a stranger (ar├н-) might fit with that. By contrast Thieme construes ary├бс╕е with vay├║n─Бni, in two somewhat different ways: Fremdling (1938, p. 41) тАЬтАж kennend die Ordnungen, die f├╝r den Fremdling gelten,тАЭ later corrected in Unters. (1949, 22 n. 1) to тАЬтАж kennend die Geheimnisse des Fremden.тАЭ The end of p─Бda c tav├бsam ├бtavy─Бn#, with the s-stem adj. followed by a (negated) comparative to the same root, nicely echoes the end of 3c with the same configuration but the comparative not negated: tav├бsas t├бv─лy─Бni. The employment of longer and shorter forms of the comparative (i.e., with or without the linking vowel - ─л-) allows the phrases to make an almost exact metrical match – except that the cadence of 5c is faulty (… -sam ├бtavy─Бn), with a light syllable at the beginning (and in fact 5 light syllables in a row (тАж -i tav├бsam a-), starting right before the caesura and continuing through the break and into the cadence. As in the paired vss. 3-4 the metrical disturbance may call attention to the formulaic match. ├бtavy─Бn also picks up k─лr├бyaс╕е тАШ(even) the weakтАЩ in 4c semantically.

In d the pres. part. kс╣г├бyantam is rendered by both Renou and Thieme (Fremdl.) as if it belongs to тИЪkс╣гi тАШdwellтАЩ (тАЬqui r├йsidesтАЭ and тАЬтАж [dich,] der da wohntтАЭ), but the part. to the root pres. of that root is kс╣гiy├бnt-; the part. here must belong to тИЪkс╣г─Б тАШrule overтАЩ (them. pres. kс╣г├бyati). Geldner may be trying to have it both ways with his тАЬder тАж thront,тАЭ if my German dictionaries are correct in glossing thronen as тАЬsit enthroned.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhat is to be proclaimed, Viс╣гс╣Зu, of you, when you save. I am ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa? Conceal not from us yourreal form, although you have engaged under a different form in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Viс╣гс╣Зu is said to have aided Vasiс╣гс╣нha inbattle under an assumed form, and, when questioned, is reported to have said: I am ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa (┼Ыipayotrarasmaya ucyate tair─Бviс╣гс╣нo bhavati: Nirukta 5.7-8). ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa = objectionable or unobjectionable. In thepreceding с╣Ыca and the с╣Ыca 7 of the preceding s┼лkta, the world is explained: penetrated, or clothed with rays oflight, ra┼Ыmibhir ariс╣гс╣нa, the radiant, the splendid; it normally means, a man naturally without prepuce; just as aman is so denuded, so is Viс╣гс╣Зu, according to his own declaration, uncovered by radiance– tejas─Бan─Бcch─Бditaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Was (this speech) of yours to be disregarded, when you proclaimed of yourself: тАЬI am ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нaтАЭ?
Do not hide away this shape from us, when you have appeared in another form in the clash.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Exactly what this vs. is trying to tell us is unclear. Most tr. and comm. take paric├бkс╣гya- as referring to something blameworthy (tadelnswert); so, e.g., Geldner (тАЬWas war an dir zu tadeln тАж?тАЭ), Oldenberg, Hoffmann (Injunc. 78-79). But the other example of this gerundive in VI.52.14 modifies v├бcas- specifically and seems to mean тАШto be disregarded, overlookedтАЩ: m─Б╠Бvo v├бc─Бс╣Гsi paric├бkс╣гy─Бс╣Зi vocam тАЬlet me not speak words to you that can be disregarded.тАЭ Esp. because the verb in the dependent cl.

belongs to тИЪvac, pf. vavakс╣г├й, it seems reasonable to supply тАШspeechтАЩ here as well.

The point seems to be that we should have paid attention when he called himself ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa, and that even when he appears in other form(s), he should not keep the form of ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa concealed from us, any more than we should not notice the name.

But what these statements are in service of, I have no idea – and the hymn ends here (save for the repeated vs. 7, which, however, makes a point of addressing Viс╣гс╣Зu as ┼Ъipiviс╣гс╣нa).

Griffith

What was there to be blamed in thee, O Visnu, when thou declaredst, I am Sipivista?
Hide not this form from us, nor keep it secret, since thou didst wear another shape in battle.

Was war an dir zu tadeln, Vishnu, als du von dir verk├╝ndest: “Ich bin Sipivista”? Verbirg diese Gestalt nicht vor uns, wenn du im Kampfe in anderer Gestalt erschienen bist!

Was war an dir, o Vischnu, zu verbergen, als du erkl├дrtest ┬╗├Зipivischta bin ich?┬л Verbirg vor uns nicht diese deine Sch├╢nheit, wenn andere Gestalt im Kampf du annahmst.

May these my songs of eulogy exalt thee. Preserve us evermore, ye Gods, with blessings.
